The February 26th Incident Shocked the World: The Full Picture of the Japanese Coup; Suicide of Rebel Generals Adds to the Tragedy; Okada Escapes and Donates Property

Tokyo

On February 26, an unprecedented rebellion suddenly occurred in Tokyo. At that time, the authorities, considering the serious nature of the incident, prohibited all reports except for the official announcement. However, on the 22nd, the scope of this report was slightly relaxed. According to reports, the twenty officers, including Captain Nonaka, who had been discharged, participated in this rebellion. The troops involved were parts of the 3rd Guards Regiment, the 1st Infantry Regiment, the 3rd Infantry Regiment, and the 7th Field Heavy Artillery Regiment, totaling more than 1,400 non-commissioned officers and soldiers. Several civilians, such as Ikki Kita and Shūmei Okawa, also participated. They initially attacked the Prime Minister's official residence, the residence of the Minister of the Imperial Household Saitō, the private residence of the Inspector General of Military Education Watanabe, the private residence of the Finance Minister Takahashi, the residence of the Grand Chamberlain Suzuki, the dormitory of the former Minister of the Imperial Household Makino, the Yubara Itoya Hotel, and the Tokyo Asahi Shimbun. The three senior officials, Saitō, Takahashi, and Watanabe, were assassinated and killed, and the Grand Chamberlain Suzuki was seriously injured. Prime Minister Okada escaped by having his brother-in-law, Colonel Matsuo, die in his place. Count Makino also escaped unharmed. The rebel troops then occupied the high ground in Nagata-cho, Kojimachi Ward, centering on the Prime Minister's official residence and the newly built Diet building. A state of emergency was declared at 3:00 AM on the 27th, and the 1st and 2nd Guards Divisions were mobilized. Troops from nearby areas such as Sakura, Mito, Utsunomiya, Takasaki, and Matsumoto were successively sent to Tokyo to maintain order and take charge of security. At the same time, various means were used to suppress the rebel troops, and the rebel army surrendered without firing a shot on the afternoon of the 29th. Among the rebel officers, Captain Nonaka committed suicide, Captain Kono committed suicide, and most of the others, such as Muranaka, Isobe, and Okawa, as well as civilian participants, were detained in the garrison prison. As for the surrendered soldiers, they were separately detained in various districts. However, more than 1,320 of the soldiers were released from detention on March 18. As a result of this incident, the Okada cabinet resigned en masse. The mandate to form a cabinet was temporarily given to Prince Konoe, but he declined, so Foreign Minister Hirota was ordered to form a cabinet. After great difficulty, it was established on March 9, taking on the heavy responsibility of resolving the extraordinary situation. Furthermore, due to the occurrence of this ominous incident, six army elders, such as Hayashi, Mazaki, Abe, Araki, Minami, and Kawashima, felt responsible and resigned from their current positions. Although this unprecedented rebellion has been quelled, its shadow remains, such as the suicide of Major Amano, the injury of Major Katakura, and the suicide of Captain Aoshima and his wife. Many tragic stories are included in this account. (22nd Allied Press)

Tokyo

Prime Minister Okada, who was attacked by rebel soldiers at 5:40 AM on February 26, the day the incident broke out, was able to escape because his brother-in-law, Colonel Matsuo, died in his place, saving his life. It is said that Prime Minister Okada was hiding in a closet in the inner room and was able to leave the official residence on the afternoon of the 27th, disguised among the mourners. His escape was described in a statement issued by Secretary Fukuda, which has already been reported. Since the incident, Prime Minister Okada has been living in seclusion in his Yodobashi residence, being extremely cautious, praying for the repose of the souls of the victims, and living a lonely life. It is said that he will donate all of his property to the Matsuo family and the families of the police officers who died, to express his gratitude. (22nd Allied Press)

Rebel Soldiers Redeem Themselves Through Merit: Sent to Serve in Manchuria

Nanjing

It was previously reported on March 19 that more than 1,320 soldiers involved in the incident were questioned, released from detention, and ordered to return to their original units. Now, they live in the barracks with ordinary soldiers. Since most of these troops are to be sent to serve in Manchuria, the various units to which they belong must begin training. Some have been assigned to important duties and are treated the same as ordinary soldiers. Fortunately, the soldiers all know their mistake and deeply regret their previous actions. They are determined to wash away their shame in Manchuria and are now working with enthusiasm. (22nd Allied Press)

Memorial Service Held for Saitō's Remains

Nanjing

The official funeral of Saitō Makoto, the former Minister of the Interior who died in the February 26th incident, was held at Honganji Temple in Tsukiji on the 22nd. The ceremony was extremely solemn and tragic. More than 700 wreaths were presented from various quarters. At 9:40 AM that day, his remains were escorted out of his residence by his family members. Funeral Committee Chairman Kodama and others participated in the procession. Members of the Japan Boy Scout League and a naval honor guard commanded by Colonel Hara also participated. The ceremony began at 10:30 AM, with the participation of Prime Minister Hirota, other cabinet members, naval admirals such as Suetsugu, Nakamura, Nomura, Kobayashi, Kato, and many other dignitaries from the political and financial circles and various fields. From 1:30 PM to 2:00 PM, a farewell ceremony was held for the general public. (22nd Allied Press)

Nanjing

The remains of the late Japanese Finance Minister Takahashi Korekiyo are scheduled to be cremated at Honganji Temple in Tsukiji, Tokyo, on the 26th of this month, following Buddhist rites. However, since Tokyo is currently under martial law, all procedures must be approved by the Martial Law Headquarters before they can be finalized. (22nd China United Press)

Random Notes on Rural Life

— Edited by Yu Qingtang

The Burden of Land Tax on Farmers in the Southeastern Countryside of Wuxi — Weng Zushan

1. Not Scratching the Itch

In the process of the collapse of the rural economy, "land tax" has also played a huge role in destruction. In the past, most scholars focused on studying the amount of tax and surcharges. Their pens rarely touched the "deep-rooted abuses" of the collection system, which is a big mistake. The rate of increase in surcharges is indeed alarming, but if we look at the farmer's extra expenses, we will find that this "invisible surcharge" often exceeds the visible surcharge several times! Therefore, to understand the reality of harsh levies and extortion, in addition to observing tangible figures, we must look for the methods of collection and the process of collection. For several years, what we have heard is nothing more than: "Surcharges are overlapping, and the people cannot bear it," "The people feel the pain most deeply from surcharges," "There are many land tax surcharges in various provinces... causing the peasants great suffering," and so on. In fact, none of them are scratching the itch!

The nature of Chinese farmers is docile. Although they are getting thinner year by year, the relief of "not owing the imperial grain above and not owing private debts below" is still what every farmer dreams of. Now the land tax surcharge in Wuxi has increased to 1.6 times the regular tax, and they still "pawn and mortgage to repay," with absolutely no complaints! Only this "invisible surcharge" has no fixed amount and is left to the extortion of the tax collectors, making it impossible to escape! A young farmer once said: "I think the 'Tu Zheng' who eats five liters of rice per mu of farmer's land should be considerate of our poor people. Who knew that he would collude with the village chief and do all kinds of evil, even making a big profit on the payment of grain to the state. With such insatiable greed, even if we shed all our sweat and blood, working like cattle and horses all our lives, we cannot afford to support them!" This is indeed the cry of the majority of the exploited. The extortion of the tax collectors should not be ignored any longer!

2. General Observations

According to what I know—Guonan Township, Wuxi—whether it is "self-assessment and deposit" or paid on behalf of the Tu Zheng, the extra expenses are always unavoidable. The exact amount of money and grain to be paid can only be known after seeing the "receipt" (notice), and the receipt is in the hands of the Gang Zheng. Often, several months after the start of the land tax collection, the Tu Zheng's receipt has not yet been issued. This does not pose a difficulty for literate landlords and merchants—they can go to the grain counter to copy the numbers themselves. But ordinary farmers have absolutely no way to do it and must beg the Tu Zheng in every way. Usually, the farmer's money and grain are handled and paid on behalf of the Tu Zheng. Or they advance the money first and then charge the farmers double. The vicious Tu Zheng is even more extortionate, with no standards at all. Not only is the receipt not issued, but even the serial number cannot be obtained. The honest and simple farmers think that once the money has been paid, everything is done. How would they ever think that they would have to face a lawsuit for back taxes after one or two years? There are countless examples of this kind of "the debt is not owed by the people, and the money is not received by the government." In addition to "floating receipts" and "secret receipts," there are also large extra demands. The expenditure is more than one item a year, and it is not just the Tu Zheng who can extort money from the farmers. According to the usual situation (although the farmers are unable to pay, they have come to regard it as a standard), the "Qu Shu" and "Tu Zheng" each collect two units from the farmers every year: one or two liters of rice per mu at rice harvest time, and one or two liters of wheat per mu at wheat harvest time. In years when the price of rice and wheat is low, cash is collected instead, with the principle that it should not be less than the highest price of rice and wheat. As for the vicious ones who collect five or six liters per mu or only collect white rice and not wheat, it is also often heard. Here are two more points to note: First, the so-called one or two liters of rice and wheat per mu per year is not an absolute number. Generally, for those with more than ten mu, the odd numbers are not counted, and those with less than ten mu often exceed this number. And 63% of the farmers here have less than ten mu. Second, the amount of extortion is proportional to the distance from the towns. The closer to the city, the less is collected. The farther away from the city, the more is collected. Less is collected in the market towns, and more is collected in the villages. As for "remote and backward areas" or in three-family villages, "heaven is high and the emperor is far away," and there is even more "lawlessness"!

These are general observations.

In addition to oral and scattered materials, I also conducted a simple investigation. This investigation covered nine households with 54.5 mu of land. The nominal regular and surcharge taxes totaled 32 yuan, 8 jiao, 1 fen, and 7 li (Note 1). The actual expenditure was 75 yuan and 5 jiao in legal tender, 2 shi, 4 dou, and 8 sheng of brown rice, and 1 shi, 8 dou, and 5 sheng of wheat, equivalent to 26 yuan, 6 jiao, and 1 fen in legal tender (Note 2). The total was 102 yuan, 1 jiao, and 1 fen. The actual expenditure was more than 8 times the regular tax and more than 3 times the regular and surcharge taxes. The amount of the floating receipt was slightly less than 3.5 times the surcharge. Below are some actual examples:

From this statistic, we can see how alarming the farmer's land tax expenditure per mu is! But what is the government's actual income?

Note 1: Wuxi has flat fields, polder fields, and shoal fields. The tax is based on the standard of flat fields, at 1.0169 yuan per mu. The rest are less than 1 yuan. There are no flat fields in these 50+ mu, so the average is only 6 jiao and 2 li per mu.

Note 2: Today's market price of brown rice is 7-8 yuan per dan, now calculated at 7 yuan. Wheat is 7 yuan per jiao per dan, but at harvest time it is only 4 yuan and 5 jiao, so it is now calculated at 5 yuan.

The Ethiopian Government Sends a Note to Geneva: The League of Nations Should Mediate a Peace Agreement; Based on the Spirit of the Covenant, Respect Territorial Integrity; Request Effective Cessation of Italian Army's Brutal Acts

Thirteen-Nation Committee to Meet Today

London

The League of Nations Thirteen-Nation Committee is scheduled to meet at 10:30 AM on Monday, at which time a new Italian-Ethiopian peace agreement can be restarted. (21st National News Agency)

London

The Ethiopian government yesterday sent a note to the Secretary-General of the League of Nations, Avenol, expressing acceptance of the cessation of hostilities between Italy and Ethiopia. The Ethiopian Minister to France, Gedamu Haile Mariam, came here from Paris yesterday to prepare to attend the League of Nations Council's Thirteen-Nation Committee. Another note was sent to Avenol, denying the talk of direct negotiations between Italy and Ethiopia, and stating that reports that Italian troops had recently broken through Ethiopian defenses were also untrue. It said, "Six months after the start of the war, although the Italian army is brutal, the Ethiopian people have not yielded. Their determination to fight the enemy is even stronger. Rumors that the people of various parts of Ethiopia do not hold a unified attitude towards Italy are also groundless." The note also stated that the Ethiopian government has quickly expressed its acceptance of the peace proposal put forward by the Thirteen-Nation Committee. The Italian government's reply only agreed in principle. The Ethiopian government specifically requested the Council to ask Italy again whether it was prepared to "respect Ethiopia's territorial integrity and conclude peace with Ethiopia 'within the framework of the League of Nations and in the spirit of the Covenant.'" (22nd Havas)

London

The Ethiopian Minister to France, Gedamu Haile Mariam, also sent a note to the Secretary-General of the League of Nations, Avenol, stating that after Ethiopia was subjected to aggression, the member states of the League of Nations unanimously condemned Italy's acts of aggression. However, Italy turned a deaf ear and continued to bomb Ethiopia and foreign aid teams, and used poison gas to kill innocent civilians. The Ethiopian government hereby requested the Council to take necessary measures to stop these brutal acts. (22nd Havas)

On the Northern and Southern Fronts: Ethiopian Army Launches a Large-Scale Counteroffensive; The City of Jijiga is Bombed by the Italian Air Force; Incendiary Bombs Rain Down, Causing Numerous Casualties

A report from General Badoglio, Commander-in-Chief of the Italian forces in East Africa, received in Rome, only mentioned that the activities on the two fronts were very lively. It is reported that the Ethiopian army on both fronts began attacking the Italian army's lines of communication yesterday. A total of two large armies participated. This morning at 7:30, 19 large bombers suddenly flew to the city of Jijiga, northeast of Harar, soaring in the blue sky and dropping thousands of incendiary bombs on the town. According to palace officials, the Italian air force is still dropping gas bombs. (21st Havas)

Severe Flooding in the Eastern United States: Followed by a Blizzard; Relief Work is Difficult; Material Losses Reach 500 Million Yuan; 300,000 Homeless

Pittsburgh, USA: At a time of severe flooding, a blizzard has struck today, making it difficult for relief workers to try to prevent epidemics in this and dozens of other cities. The filth left behind after the floodwaters recede is very dangerous, so residents and relief workers are doing their best to clear it away at night in the darkness of ankle-deep snow. The military and government agencies are trying to restore the water supply and disinfect the reservoirs. In rural areas where the water has not yet receded, food and medicine are transported by car and plane. The authorities estimate that the losses in Pennsylvania will be between US$250 million and US$500 million. (21st National News Agency)

New York

The peak of the floods in the United States is rolling downstream today. In the fourteen eastern states, at least 209 people have died, including men, women, the elderly, and children. 320,000 people have been left homeless. The minimum estimate of property losses is US$250 million, but Pennsylvania authorities have announced that even that state alone is more than that amount. The city of Hartford in Connecticut is still raining today, but the water has receded slightly at night. There appears to be new danger in northern New York State, as heavy rains have resumed, the snow has melted, and mountain torrents are flowing down, flooding both banks. Many industrial areas along the Merrimack River in northeastern Massachusetts have been flooded. Many of the electric plants there have also been shut down. The number of homeless and unemployed is countless. Fortunately, it seems that the dangerous period has passed tonight in most other places. (21st National News Agency)

Portsmouth, USA: The Ohio River continues to flow south, flooding the cities of Portsmouth, Gallipolis, Ironton, Ohio, and Plaisented and Huntington, West Virginia. Because residents there had precautions, they have all carried their belongings to higher ground, and relief work has been prepared early. (21st National News Agency)

The American Industrial Reform Association: Submits Recommendations to Roosevelt; How to Avoid a Recession

New York

The Industrial Reform Association today submitted a report to President Roosevelt, suggesting ways to avoid future recessions. The report opposes managing industry by government decree, such as the now defunct National Recovery Administration, but advocates legislation to control wages and prices to stabilize the American economic system. Unlimited competition can lead to unequal income, and if this continues, a more serious economic crisis will inevitably occur than this one. As for how to avoid it, the report suggests the following:

* Set minimum wages and maximum working hours to avoid labor price competition.

* Use collective bargaining to maintain wages above the minimum.

* Set minimum prices.

* Allow commercial organizations to enforce fair practices.

* Study the problem of technological unemployment.

* For the sake of labor protection, impose quantitative restrictions on imports and implement effective anti-dumping laws. (21st National News Agency)

Western Border News

Travelogue of Qinghai (Continued): A Scene of Devil Dancing

The annual Devil Dance was about to begin, and we were swept along with the crowd to the plaza on the right. We secured a carpeted seat in front of the temple, where there was already no empty space in the arena. The audience was seated by soldiers wielding leather whips, and over a dozen photographers with cameras had already climbed onto the rooftops. Several foreigners with movie cameras were also mixed in.

The sound of drums and gongs rose, and the crowd grew silent. Four dancing skeletons appeared in the center of the plaza, followed by comical big-headed monks, ferocious ox-headed and horse-faced figures, and lively little deer. Each dance scene progressed with the rhythm of the drums and gongs, advancing and retreating. In the final scene, a devil made of tsampa (roasted barley flour) was placed on a plate in the center of the arena. A bull demon king-like deity, after a series of dances, knelt before the devil, raised a dagger in his right hand, and hacked the devil in the plate into several pieces. Several deer deities then shook their heads and wagged their tails around the scattered tsampa, celebrating their victory. This is a story from Tibetan religion about eliminating devils who destroy religion. Most monasteries have similar, slightly different versions of this dance.

The local Han Chinese thus associated this with "slaying Nian." "Nian" refers to Nian Gengyao, who pacified the west in the early Qing dynasty. He executed eight lamas at the Tar Temple, who are now buried in front of the "Small Golden Tile Temple," marked by eight pagodas. The lamas in the temple have hated him for generations. Each year during the Devil Dance, they mold him into a devil of tsampa, dismembering him as revenge. Therefore, the devil represents Nian, and this scene of the dance is called "slaying Nian."

Tourists Swarm

Inside the temple, we only saw swirling dust and a sea of people. According to the temple's estimates, the total number of attendees exceeded 30,000, of which 60% were Tibetans, 20% were Mongols, 20% were Han and Hui people, and 7 or 8 were foreigners taking photos. This year, because the Panchen Lama was residing here, the Mongol and Tibetan people had a triple purpose: to pilgrimage, to pay homage to the Living Buddha, and to see the lantern display. Many were Mongols from Alashan and Qaidam, and Tibetans from Yushu and Nangqian, who had traveled from afar, making the event even more lively than in previous years.

Their tents filled the valleys for ten miles around. The narrow mountain paths were packed with a throng of people. Many Tibetan men wore new silk robes, with heavy silver bowls and headdresses adorned with coral and shells on their backs. Many Mongols leading camels were interspersed among them, creating a unique atmosphere.

From Yuershal to Tar Temple, the mountainside along the several-mile road was lined with merchants' tents. The Mongol and Tibetan people crowded here, packed like sardines. Copper and iron tools, fabrics, jewelry, colorful paper, and steaming snacks on the stalls all sold at ten times their usual price.

On the morning of the 15th, we went up the mountain for some fresh air. Groups of dozens of Mongol and Tibetan men and women were already worshiping on the mountain paths, prostrating themselves until they were covered in dirt, showing their utmost sincerity.

Today, the Panchen Lama chanted scriptures in front of the main hall. Three thousand five hundred lamas clapped and stamped their feet, discussing the scriptures. An entranced audience prostrated towards the Panchen Lama's shadow from the stone steps hundreds of paces away. Many kneeled down even without seeing the shadow, and countless weak individuals stood behind them, their foreheads unable to touch the stone steps at the temple entrance, making their long journeys seem in vain.

Beautiful Butter Lamps

Tonight is the Lantern Festival. Wherever there is Lamaism, the butter lamps of Tar Temple are considered the most exquisite and magnificent, so the Mongol and Tibetan people are proud to have a glimpse of the butter lamp stands.

The butter lamps are manufactured far in advance, half a year prior. The artisans who make the butter lamps take 1,500 catties of butter from the temple and quietly create them in a secret room, where no one is allowed to observe.

After sunset on the Lantern Festival, they display the magnificent butter lamps in a tent – a canopy – embroidered with Buddha images, allowing people to admire them. The Panchen Lama is the first to view them, and then it is our turn. In the darkness, two lamas led the way with lanterns. One lama used a whip to clear a path through the crowd, leading us directly to the shimmering lights on the right side of the Great Golden Tile Temple.

Two large butter lamp displays were placed on the east and west sides, like colorful bas-relief archways towering to the top of the twenty-foot-high canopy. Below, a row of bright butter lamps illuminated a vivid Buddha statue in the center of the archway. On either side of the Buddha, pavilions, towers, trees, flowers, people riding horses, and people strolling were all arranged in recreational scenes. The clothing of the figures and the colors of the flowers and trees were bright and pleasing to the eye. The exquisite and lifelike workmanship was like the real thing. Especially under the flickering lamplight, it almost felt like being in a wax museum in Paris. Most strikingly, a pair of winged bombers hovered in the sky above the ornate buildings, and a blooming cannon was firing on the ground, seemingly symbolizing the ominous signs of war.

The crowd was too dense, so we hastily retreated, following the lama around the Great Golden Tile Temple. There were seven or eight places along the way with smaller butter lamps, but the workmanship and colors were much poorer. Most had only a triangular panel and a two- or three-foot-tall Buddha statue. The crowds were not as dense here, and the sincere old women were kowtowing towards them.

The festival will be over tomorrow. At eight o'clock in the morning, we took the original car back. The tents along the road were being dismantled in succession, and the crowds were heading back in all directions.

The Plight of Chaozhou-Meizhou People Deceived into Going to Siam: Five to Six Hundred People Detained in Siam, Now Imprisoned Awaiting Bail and Release

Shantou Correspondence: In recent years, industries and commerce in various parts of Southeast Asia have been in decline, and many overseas Chinese have returned home after losing their jobs. However, after returning home, these people still face unemployment, hunger, and cold due to the collapse of the rural economy in their hometowns. Therefore, they still seek opportunities to go to Southeast Asia. Last year, the prices of rubber and tin in Southeast Asia slightly increased, and industries and commerce showed signs of recovery. Overseas Chinese who heard the news vied to go there. Unscrupulous merchants on general ships and in hotels seized the opportunity to cheat and profit. They manipulated the prices of ship tickets and sent people around to deceive overseas Chinese, concealing passengers to various ports in Southeast Asia. As a result, they were repeatedly discovered by the colonial governments of Southeast Asia, leading to wrongful imprisonment. Recently, the number of impoverished overseas Chinese from Chaozhou and Meizhou who were deceived into going to Siam and ended up in prison has reached four to five hundred people. The details are as follows:

Since Siam implemented its immigration law, overseas Chinese going to Siam have been hesitant due to the cumbersome residency procedures. Ship companies and hotels have suffered from reduced revenue as a result. Therefore, they colluded to cheat and defraud. First, customer heads and escorts were sent out from various hotels to the Chaozhou area to falsely claim that the Siamese immigration regulations had been changed, that the residency fee and import license fee had been reduced to 50 baht, and that no other inspection procedures were required. If they were transported by these people from Shantou to Siam, they would only be charged 70-80 yuan per person for a safe passage. As a result, many villagers in the hinterland who intended to go to Southeast Asia but were unaware of the details were deceived. They borrowed from relatives and friends or sold their property to raise funds and went to Shantou with the customer heads and escorts to wait for ships to Siam. Once the money was paid, they were taken to the ship and hidden in bamboo baskets or in the corners of the cabins, coal piles, and cargo holds. The unscrupulous merchants only cared about money and did not care about the safety of the deceived passengers. On the 12th of last month, a certain ship represented by a certain company in Shantou sailed from Shantou to Siam. On the 20th of this month, upon arrival in Siam, the head of the Siamese Public Security Bureau, based on a report that the ship was secretly carrying a large number of passengers to escape entry, immediately dispatched more than 60 police officers, immigration officials, and undercover agents to inspect the ship. As a result, more than 180 people were apprehended. On the 29th of this month, a certain ship arrived in Siam again and was subjected to a strict inspection, resulting in the discovery of another 423 people. When the ship arrived in Siam, all the passengers were arrested. Due to the large number of passengers, the order was extremely chaotic. The inspection time for the ship lasted for more than 20 hours. Except for a small number of passengers with entry and exit permits who were fortunate enough to leave, the rest were not allowed to take a step beyond the bounds. The next day, after another inspection by immigration officials, those who were trying to sneak into the country were arrested and sentenced by the Siamese court to a fine of 200 baht each. However, because everyone admitted to evading entry, the punishment was reduced by half to 100 baht. Those who could not pay the fine were imprisoned for 100 days in lieu of the fine, and then deported back to their country upon completion of their sentence. After this tragedy occurred, overseas Chinese in Siam sought to rescue them. The Siamese Chinese General Chamber of Commerce once held a meeting to discuss relief measures and initially intended to pay the fines on their behalf to get them out of prison. However, because the number of detainees reached 500-600 people, requiring more than 60,000 baht, and because of the current economic downturn, fundraising was difficult, so no agreement could be reached. As a result, it was decided to publish a notice explaining the difficulties of the Chamber of Commerce and asking relatives and friends of the detainees to find ways to rescue them, and to translate the Siamese immigration law and send it to the authorities in Shantou, Guangzhou, and Haikou to inform the public and avoid being deceived. At the same time, the General Chamber of Commerce sent letters to various shipping companies, warning the ship staff not to deceive overseas Chinese into going abroad.

Page 7

Japanese Troops Stationed at Tianjin Main Station Affects Railway Freight; Pseudo-Police Inspection of Passengers Leaving the Pass Also Affects the Business of the Beining Railway

Tianjin Correspondence: Since last winter, when a Japanese military police unit was stationed at the Tianjin Main Station of the Jinpu Railway to monitor train operations, it has been several months now and they have not yet withdrawn. The military police unit consists of five people, occupying half of the waiting room on the second platform of the main station as a temporary office, where they eat and sleep. Whenever freight trains arrive at the station, they go out to inspect the number and number of the cars and record them one by one. They are somewhat lenient with trains coming from the north, but they are unwilling to let trains going south pass easily unless the number of cars matches the number coming from the north, and even then they generally only allow trains with no more than fifteen cars to pass. At the same time, the Tianjin Main Station freight yard must store about thirty freight cars every day, which makes the Jinpu Railway's train operations extremely inconvenient. Recently, with the arrival of spring, freight transport is booming, and goods transported south are piling up in the freight yard like mountains. Freight owners have repeatedly urged the railway authorities to transport the goods, but because the scheduling is restricted by the Japanese military police, they cannot load as desired. The Jinpu Railway's Tianjin Office has negotiated with the Japanese side on this matter several times, but the Japanese side claims to have received secret reports, so this difficulty in foreign affairs is difficult to resolve in a short time. Earlier this month, the pseudo-National Border Police Team of Yuguan banned Chinese from leaving the pass and issued a new law requiring all passengers leaving the pass to pay 20 yuan for a special identification card. Those who leave the pseudo-national territory within one month can get 19 yuan back from the Yuguan Datong Company with the original card. The Beining Railway Bureau believes that this measure affects its business and has sent a letter to the Oriental Travel Agency for negotiation. Igarashi Fangji, the manager of the pseudo-Yuguan Datong Company, came to Tianjin for this matter to contact the Beining Railway and explained the process of handling this matter, seeking to avoid misunderstandings. The Beining Railway Bureau requested the company to consult with the pseudo-National Border Police to change the method in order to facilitate passengers and avoid losses to the railway's business. At the same time, passengers who were unaware of the new restrictions on entry outside the pass would not be stranded on the way. After Igarashi returned, the Oriental Travel Agency negotiated again, and the pseudo-Border Police began to be less strict in restricting passengers leaving the pass than before. Currently, they have adopted a quick method. Passengers taking the Ping-Shen through train get off the train at Yuguan and line up on the platform. The pseudo-police quickly inspect and interrogate them within the 40 minutes of the train's stop. At the same time, staff from the Datong Company sell exit permits. Upper-class people are charged one yuan per permit according to the old rules, while small vendors and laborers are still charged 20 yuan per permit to restrict entry. If the inspection is not completed when the train is about to depart, they are allowed to take the next pseudo-Fengshan Railway Shen-Yu through train to leave the pass. However, the Oriental Travel Agency and the Beining Railway Bureau believe that this is still not a convenient way for passengers, so they hope that the pseudo-police and people from the Datong Company can inspect passengers and sell exit permits on the train to save time and avoid delaying passengers' journeys. The station where the procedures will be handled is still under study. The pseudo-Border Police Team and the Datong Company have no objections to this principle and are waiting for their opinions to match before implementing it. (20th)

Taiwan Recruiting Chinese Laborers to Open Mines; Many Workers from Wenzhou Apply; Japanese Side Also Sends Personnel to Fujian to Recruit Widows

Xiamen Correspondence: In recent weeks, many workers from Wenzhou have been traveling to Taiwan from Xiamen by ship, reportedly in response to an invitation from the Jilong Jin Guishan mining area in Taiwan. The mining area has been mined by Japanese entrepreneurs for gold, coal, and other minerals since the beginning of the Republic of China. Recently, due to the needs of the so-called emergency period, the mining has been intensified and there is a great need for labor. In addition to declaring that they will increase wages, the mine owners have ordered Chinese workers in the mining area to invite their relatives and friends to work, and have also sent personnel to Fujian to recruit workers, especially widows. As a result, many Japanese ships have traveled to Taiwan, carrying large numbers of workers from Wenzhou who have applied for the job, some bringing their families with them. It is said that gold mine workers can earn 50 Japanese yen per month, while coal workers can earn 30 Japanese yen per month. All food is paid for by the workers themselves, and travel expenses are also paid by the workers themselves. The entrance permit fee for workers going to Taiwan is about 13 yuan, while it is slightly higher for merchants, about 2 or 3 yuan more. Since the New Year, more than a thousand people have traveled to Taiwan in an endless stream. Many workers from Fuqing have also been exported from Fuzhou. Recently, it was discovered that people in Anxi were distributing leaflets recruiting workers to go to Taiwan. It is said that those who work in the mining area must first undergo training. (March 22nd)

Henan Province Planting Trees Along the Zhangwei and Qi Rivers; Poor Results from Past Tree Planting; Construction Department Seeking Remedial Measures

Kaifeng Correspondence: Tree planting along the Zhang, Wei, and Qi rivers was carried out once last spring, with a total of 2,139,187 trees planted. Because there is a lot of good farmland on both banks, and the government is short on funds, it cannot buy it at market price. People are unwilling to let the trees survive due to their own interests, resulting in only over 150,000 trees surviving. In order to remedy this, the Construction Department reduced the width of the afforestation area to 50 meters last winter, stipulating that from November 15th to December 15th, the rivers should be cleared and measured in sections for afforestation, with a wooden stake inserted every kilometer to calculate the number of trees to be planted and the number of acres and labor required. From December 16th to January 15th of this year, the willow cuttings that should be planted were inserted. From February 1st to March 15th, persimmon, paper mulberry, yellow ash, ailanthus, chinaberry, walnut, cypress, poplar, ash, and other miscellaneous trees were planted. In addition to dispatching ten technicians from the Kaifeng First Agricultural and Forestry Bureau, Xinyang Second Agricultural and Forestry Bureau, Nanyang Third Agricultural and Forestry Bureau, Luoyang Fourth Agricultural and Forestry Bureau, and Huixian Fifth Agricultural and Forestry Bureau to various counties to supervise and guide, the county magistrate of the local area was also assigned as the chief supervisor, the section chiefs along the river were assigned as supervisors, and the afforestation area was divided into sections of every five or ten miles, with the section chiefs assigning the baojia chiefs as section leaders, and each team consisting of 50 afforestation laborers, with the section chiefs assigning team leaders. Currently, each county has reported completion. Except for mountainous areas such as Shexian, Tangyin, and Linxian, where planting is done according to the terrain, the rest are planted using the square planting method. The afforestation locations and lengths are recorded below:

(C) Anyang, from Guantai to the east of Lao Fengle Town Village, 26.4 kilometers long, planted on the south bank. (D) Linjin, from the west of Yezhen Village in the west of the county to the north of Shen Xiaotun, about 44.6 kilometers long, planted on the south bank. (E) Neihuang, from the west of Huang Gan Gu Village to the east of Lanzhuang, 4 kilometers long, planted on the south bank.

Wei River: (A) Bo'ai, from Liucun at the diversion of the Qin River in the west of the county to the border between Han Gao Village and Xiuwu in the east of the county, 28.6 kilometers long, planted on the south bank. (B) Wuzhi, from Zhucun in the west of the county to Xiao Li Village in the north of the county, 15.4 kilometers long, planted on the east bank. (C) Xiuwu, from Nanxie Village in the southwest of the county to Machang Village in the northeast, bordering Huojia, 33.6 kilometers long, planted on the south bank. (D) Huojia, from Liuqiao Village entering the county in the west to Dong'an Village in the east, 18 kilometers long, planted on the south bank. The above four counties are located upstream of the Wei River, collectively known as the Dan River. (E) Xinxiang, from the north of the Dan River mouth to Quli Village, about 25 kilometers long, planted on the south bank. (F) Ji County, from Quli Village to the east of Dong Ban Shuvin, bordering Junxian, 48 kilometers long, planted on the south bank. (G) Qi County, from the west of Qimen Town to Han Pu on the border of Tangyin, 85 kilometers long, planted on the east and south banks. (H) Tangyin, the Wei River has two sections in this county, one from the southwest of Wachan in the fourth district to the northeast of Weijiawan on the border of Huaxian, and one from the south of Zhu Zhuang to the north of Zhu Zhuang, both upstream and downstream within the territory of Neihuang County, 6.33 kilometers long, planted on the east bank. A Tour of the Central Hospital in Nanjing: A Towering Four-Story Building Stands Beside Zhongshan Road; Its Equipment is Comprehensive and the Number of Patients Seeking Treatment is Extremely High

Nanjing Correspondence: The Central Hospital is the leading national hospital in the capital. Under the leadership of Secretary Lu Tianmu, we were given a tour of the hospital. The following is a record of its general situation:

In 1929, after the wartime Military Medical Administration Committee was dissolved, the current hospital director, Liu Ruiheng, received a personal instruction from Chairman Chiang Kai-shek to prepare the Central Model Military Hospital as soon as possible. It was to accommodate sick and wounded soldiers while also providing medical services to the public. Immediately, fifty acres of land formerly belonging to the Banner system at the corner of Zhongshan East Road and Huangpu Road were acquired as the hospital site. On one hand, thirteen wooden prefabricated hospital buildings and X-ray machines, along with other medical equipment, were ordered from the United States. On the other hand, specialists in various fields were hired, and medical services were immediately initiated. In January 1930, another instruction was received from Chairman Chiang to rename the Central Model Military Hospital as the Central Hospital and place it under the jurisdiction of the Ministry of Health. This marked the beginning of the hospital's establishment. In the spring of 1933, a newly constructed four-story building was completed, costing one million yuan. The overseas Chinese philanthropist Hu Wenhu donated 370,000 yuan, with the remainder provided by the government. On June 18th, all departments and wards were moved into the new building. All the previously constructed wooden buildings were then converted into school buildings, dormitories, and a library.

When the hospital was first established, it only had departments of Internal Medicine, Surgery, and Ophthalmology, Otorhinolaryngology, etc. In 1933, it was divided into departments of Internal Medicine, Surgery, Obstetrics and Gynecology, Ophthalmology, Otorhinolaryngology, Dentistry, Urology, Orthopedics, Dermatology, Pediatrics, and Tuberculosis. In addition, there were attached departments of Radiology, Electrotherapy, and Laboratory. The number of beds was also expanded from 275 to 336.

The hospital building is three-dimensional, shaped like two "凸" characters joined together. It faces south from the north. The outpatient department is on the west side, with the registration area to the left and the cashier's office to the right. In the center is a bronze bust of the donor, Hu Wenhu, surrounded by railings. Above it hangs a horizontal plaque inscribed with the four characters "益在民生" (Benefit to the People's Livelihood), presented to Hu Wenhu by the National Government. This area has many seats, intended as a waiting area for patients. Moving forward from here, the medical records room is on the left. For returning patients, after completing the registration procedures, their medical records are retrieved and sent to the attending physician. All past symptoms and diagnoses are recorded, following the model of Peking Union Medical College Hospital, with the intention of preserving them for twenty to thirty years. Therefore, all medical records from the opening in 1929 to the present are preserved. This is similar to the archives of general administrative agencies. On the right is the pharmacy, staffed by more than ten pharmacists and assistants, who were busily preparing medications. Several basic solutions were also pre-prepared for immediate use. Medications for inpatients are requisitioned from the pharmacy daily by the nurses, who then distribute them to the patients. Further ahead are the various department clinics, emergency rooms, and the social services department. For poor patients, after investigation by this department, all consultation fees and examination fees can be waived. Another section is the administrative department and the infectious disease ward, which has been isolated. It currently houses fifteen patients, including two children. The conditions include tuberculosis (consumption) in eleven people, pneumonia in one person, chickenpox in one person, gonorrheal eye disease in one person, and congenital syphilis in one person. Afterwards, we visited the electrotherapy department, which has several high-frequency diathermy machines and short-wave diathermy machines. Their function is to treat pneumonia and sterilize, among other things. In addition, there are hot light lamps, which can treat muscles and improve blood flow.

The eastern part of the second floor is the X-ray room. At this time, an X-ray examination was being performed on the arm of a child, perhaps six or seven years old. The child was crying because of the change in environment, but in reality, it was no different from a regular photograph and did not involve any pain. We then visited the operating room. In the center was a bed where more than ten doctors and assistants were performing surgery on a young woman. The temperature in the room was very high, and the doctors were all wearing light clothing and masks. It was said that this was to prevent respiration from affecting the patient's affected area. We faintly heard the young woman's cries, incessant and unending. It was presumed that she had received local anesthesia, so she was still conscious. The western part of the second floor is the second and third wards. First, second, and third class wards are available. First-class wards cost eight to ten yuan per day, second-class wards cost four yuan, and third-class wards cost sixty cents. Except for two or three first-class wards that were still vacant, the others were almost completely full. When patients need something or have a request, they can press the light switch. When the red light outside the ward turns on, a small light in the nurse's office also lights up at the same time, and they immediately come to inquire, avoiding the trouble of the patient shouting. The third floor is the fourth and fifth wards, exclusively for obstetrics and general gynecology. In addition, there are nurseries and delivery rooms. The fourth floor is the sixth, seventh, and eighth wards. The eastern part is the general surgical ward, with two rooms, each with twenty-six beds. Among them, three people were in tilt tables, head down and feet up, in a suspended position. This was because their affected area was in the lower limbs. The western part is the women's internal medicine and pediatric wards, which will also be fully occupied. There are strips of red and blue cloth tightly fixed to the beds. According to a nurse, the red color indicates that the patient needs to drink more boiled water, the blue color indicates that all food and drink should be avoided, and the yellow color indicates that specially prepared food should be given. According to Mr. Lu, every morning, there may still be some space in the beds, but by the afternoon, they are all occupied. Some patients are even turned away due to lack of capacity. According to records, Nanjing, as of recently, including Gulou Hospital and the newly opened Municipal Hospital, as well as other public and private hospitals, has a total of only 906 beds, averaging one bed for every 1,100 people, leading to a supply that cannot meet demand. To alleviate the suffering of patients, it is necessary for Nanjing to add more large-scale hospitals.

According to a report by Hospital Director Liu Ruiheng, the number of patients treated at the hospital in 1930 and 1931 was 57,823. In 1932, the number of outpatients was 46,607. In 1933, the number of outpatients was 71,827. In 1934, the number of outpatients was 96,630. The number of inpatients also increased sharply each year. In 1930 and 1931, it was 5,111. In 1932, it was 4,142. In 1933, it was 4,968. In 1934, it was 6,217. The number of discharged patients in that year was the same as the above figure. The number of deaths was 472. Compared with the 4,946 discharged patients and 401 deaths in 1932, the mortality rate had decreased compared to 1933. As for the number of outpatients and discharged patients in 1935, because the hospital's annual report has not yet been published, it is impossible to speculate. However, according to recent conditions, the number of inpatients each day is around 330, and the number of outpatients is around 500, for a total of 800 people. According to this statistic, the total number of people treated throughout the year will almost exceed 200,000. However, most inpatients are long-term cases. It can be asserted that the number of patients seeking treatment this year will be at least around 150,000.

Jiang Song: Investigate the Case of Resisting Arrest for Opium

Our county is conducting a general crackdown on opium offenders. In recent days, the county government has dispatched a large number of officials to arrest over a hundred opium offenders. The other day, the county government sent Hu Guanxian to inspect the opium den of Cao Yi in Zhelin. It was learned that people with Fengxian County opium licenses were smoking inside, which was clearly illegal. While waiting to consult with the patrol officer to take them to the station, another opium addict came to smoke. Upon inspection, it was found that the soil purchase accounting form did not have blue chops, indicating that the purchase was incomplete. All were ordered to be taken to the station, and the accounts of the opium den were taken back for submission. Unexpectedly, a group of ruffians gathered and shouted, snatching Hu's official briefcase and tearing the police officer's coat. Hu immediately went to the township office and submitted a written report to the county government for handling. Recently, the county government has ordered the arrest of the perpetrators. Zhou Changhua's home in Jiaxu Township, Yizheng County.

Kunshan: Seven Bandits Sentenced to Imprisonment

The county was robbed by bandits. Zhou immediately rang the gong to call for help. Fortunately, the villagers gathered and captured eight bandits, seizing a large number of bullets. One of them, Wang Honggen, was injured while resisting arrest and later died. The remaining bandits were handed over to the county for legal action. It is now learned that the case has been investigated by the judiciary several times and a verdict has been reached. Xu Jiasheng, Xue Changgen, and Jiang Zhigao were each sentenced to eight years of imprisonment. Zhou Zhide was sentenced to five years of imprisonment. Lei Chengzhen, Ma Mingjiang, and Li Shaoqing were each sentenced to two years and six months of imprisonment.

Suzhou: Special Commissioner Sun Again Accused

Sun Danzhen, the special commissioner of party affairs in Wu County, was previously accused by more than 100 party members, including Chen Weizhi, to the provincial party headquarters for not being in line with public opinion. Upon receiving this news, Sun resigned passively and automatically, going to the Tangxi County government in Zhejiang Province to serve as a secretary. His duties were temporarily assumed by Gan Shi Jiang Hong. While the provincial party headquarters was searching for a successor, there was no shortage of people in Suzhou seeking this position. They entrusted influential people to recommend them to the provincial authorities. As a result, all failed, and Sun Danzhen was ordered to continue in his position. Unexpectedly, less than two months later, more than forty party members, including Yang Naizhi, jointly filed a complaint with the central party headquarters yesterday, listing four charges against Sun Danzhen, including perverting the law and neglecting his duties, and engaging in embezzlement and corruption. They requested that the Jiangsu Provincial Party Headquarters strictly and thoroughly investigate the matter to uphold party discipline.

Wang Peiyuan Sent to Prison for Execution

Wang Peiyuan, a lawyer from Shanghai, was accused by the plaintiff Liu Yue'e and others of theft. The Wu County District Court sentenced him to one year and six months of imprisonment. Wang appealed to the High Court, which upheld the original judgment. His application for a retrial was also rejected. He was sent to the Jiangsu Third Prison for execution yesterday (the 22nd).

Wuxi: Adding Road Surface to the Xiyi Road

Since the opening of the Xiyi Road, the Jiangnan Automobile Company has seen thriving business and annual profits. However, the road surface of the Meiyuan to Lujiang section and the Yixing to Tingqiao section was originally coal slag. Due to long-term erosion, it has been severely damaged. The company has now ordered workers to add crushed stone and coal slag. The Zhoufang Road, which extends for more than ten miles from the west of the Qiting Bridge to Gaosheng, is also being widened to three meters. There is also the Guanyang Road, which is currently under construction. This road is east of the Qiting Bridge and is more than sixty miles long. It will soon be completed.

Changzhou: Agricultural Bank Handles Seedling Loans

The Jiangsu Provincial Farmers Bank, in order to alleviate the rural situation as the spring plowing season is approaching, has allocated six million yuan to order the farmers banks in various counties to handle seedling loans. After receiving the order, the Wujin Farmers Bank immediately prepared to handle this loan. It stipulates an interest rate starting at one cent per month and is lent to various cooperatives in principle. Starting next month, the loans will be disbursed, with the deadline for repayment set after the autumn harvest. It has also been decided to handle storage and mortgage loans in the autumn of this year and transportation and sales loans in the winter.

Jiangyin: Conflict in Hou Shengzhen Investigation of Opium

Jiang Wenbao, an investigator from the Provincial Opium Prohibition Association, learned that someone was privately selling opium in the Yuhe Pharmacy in the second district of Hou Shengzhen. He telegraphed County Magistrate Yan and dispatched Shi Weigong and Wei Jitang, officials from the fourth section, to Hou. They searched the pharmacy and seized 134 taels of opium and arrested the opium trafficker Jiang Qianfu and others. Later, they went to the home of Shen Li to search, but found nothing. Afterwards, Shen Li questioned them, alarming the crowd, who shouted loudly. Investigator Jiang was beaten, but fortunately, the town's business corps rescued him and escorted him to the town office. The opium trafficker was handed over to the county for interrogation on the 21st.

Yangzhou: Gathering to Uproot Mulberry Seedlings to Protect Righteous Graves

The area from Erbandianpu on Aozi Street outside the Dongguan Gate of Yangzhou City to the former Provincial Silkworm Seed Manufacturing Institute on the old Wutai Mountain outside the Bianyimen Gate is less than two li. This area was originally a righteous burial ground with about two thousand graves. This year, the institute needed land to plant mulberry seedlings and reported to the county bureau to acquire the land. On the 20th, it dispatched more than sixty workers, carrying mulberry seedlings, to plant them, inevitably damaging the graves. The local people, seeing the graves being destroyed and bones being thrown, suddenly rang the gong and gathered hundreds of people, uprooting all the planted mulberry seedlings, making a menacing scene. Fortunately, the workers at the site saw that there were many people and retreated. On the 21st, Wang Shishan, the town leader of Shenglongzhen, in addition to reporting to the county bureau, planned to submit a statement to the civil and military halls, stating the reasons for protecting the righteous burial ground.

Nantong: Smallpox is Prevalent; Widespread Vaccination

Smallpox has broken out in areas such as Xiting in Tongyi, and deaths are quite numerous. The Nantong District Commissioner's Office has dispatched administrative guidance officer Ge Xifeng to handle the widespread implementation of vaccination. All public and private medical institutions are also uniformly vaccinating.

The Importance and Promotion of Literacy Movement (Part 2): Section Chief of the Ministry of Education

— Zhong Lingxiu

However, to implement this method, the government must make the greatest determination and use strict compulsory methods. Although some people in important positions may not have time to teach people to read, we can think of other remedies to replace them. In this way, the problem of teachers will not be a major problem. As for literacy textbooks, many are needed. It would be great if there were funds to print them. If there are no funds, literate people can each copy three copies and give them to the illiterate people they should be teaching. In this way, the textbook printing costs can also be saved. In addition, the educational administrative authorities can order students at all levels of schools to copy several copies each semester. Those who have a calligraphy class can change their calligraphy time to copying literacy textbooks. Taking into account the total number of university students, vocational school students, secondary school students, and upper primary school students across the country, tens of millions of copies can be copied each year. This is another way to remedy the shortage of literacy textbooks. In addition, the paper and brushes needed to promote literacy education can also be reused by using scrap paper and the paper used to wrap objects, as well as the back of various discarded mimeographs. If they are sorted and flattened, they can be used as paper for illiterate people to write and calculate on. So-called "waste utilization" can be used to find as many poor ways as possible to remedy the situation. There must be many things that can be utilized. In this way, there are considerable remedies for schools, teachers, textbooks, paper, brushes, etc. It is possible to save costs everywhere. Although it is not possible to save all costs, it is possible to save a large portion. Therefore, the cost problem is not very problematic. Therefore, as long as the government makes the greatest determination, strictly supervises, and mobilizes all parties to work together, the method of compulsory literacy education can be boldly implemented with swiftness and efficiency. There is no great difficulty.

The above are all active methods. In addition, passive methods should also be used to supervise them in order to remedy the shortcomings of compulsory methods. They are described separately below:

Illiterate people between the ages of sixteen and fifty must enroll in nearby community schools, literacy schools, or other literacy places within a certain period of time to receive literacy education. Those who violate this rule will be punished.

Illiterate people between the ages of sixteen and fifty must recognize the prescribed minimum number of characters within the prescribed time limit. If they still do not recognize the prescribed number of characters after the deadline, they will be punished.

Literacy verification points should be set up at all traffic intersections, city gates, train stations, and docks. Those who cannot prove that they are literate must be inspected. Those who pass the test will be allowed to pass. Those who fail the test must pay a "literacy donation" before being allowed to pass.

When hiring people for various agencies, groups, factories, companies, banks, stores, etc., they must be questioned. Illiterate people will not be hired.

After the literacy deadline has passed, drivers of cars, horse-drawn carriages, and rickshaws who are found to be illiterate will not be issued driving permits and will not be allowed to drive or pull carts.

Literacy checkpoints should be set up at the entrances to libraries, museums, educational halls, stadiums, parks, and other entertainment venues. Literate people can freely enter and exit. Illiterate people must pay a "literacy donation" or buy a ticket before being allowed to enter.

If the above active methods and passive methods are used together, the effect will be greatly enhanced. However, there will inevitably be many omissions. It is hoped that comrades who are enthusiastic about the literacy movement will make many additions. Only a few examples are listed here.

In the past two years, many provinces and cities have actively promoted the literacy movement and strictly enforced compulsory measures, with remarkable results. For example, Shanghai, Qingdao, Nanjing, Jiangsu, Fujian, Jiangxi, Hubei, and Anhui are all working very hard. In the near future, they will be able to realize their plans one by one, which is admirable! Now, the national crisis is serious and getting deeper day by day. Illiterate people who are ignorant and uninformed will not only be unable to save the country, but will also be unable to stand in the world of the twentieth century, where the superior prevails and the inferior is eliminated. We should be determined that "there is no room for illiteracy under the Three Principles of the People" and work hard to promote it actively. It is hoped that people across the country will pay attention to it and promote its success.

Wang Chonghui Arrives in Shanghai from Hong Kong Yesterday Afternoon; He Will Go to Beijing After Recovering from a Cold

Wang Chonghui, who has decided to resign from his position as a judge at the International Court of Justice in The Hague, arrived in Hong Kong on the 10th of this month. He visited Hu Zhantang, chairman of the Central Executive Committee, and other important figures in the Southwest to discuss national affairs. He arrived in Shanghai yesterday morning at 11:00 a.m. on the Italian postal ship Victoria. Mr. Wang had a slight cold en route. After disembarking, he went to the hospital to recuperate. He will go to Beijing after his body recovers. The details are as follows:

Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday Afternoon

The Victoria entered the port at 10:00 a.m. yesterday morning and docked at the China Merchants Bureau's North Wharf at 11:00 a.m. A large number of Mr. Wang's relatives and friends came to the port to welcome him. They included Secretary Tang Shixuan representing Mayor Wu, Zhou Yu, director of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs' Shanghai office, Yang Dezhao, representative of Chen Jitang in Beijing, Guo Yun'guan, president of the First Special District Court, Wang Simo, president of the Second Special District Court, Xu Weizhen, president of the Second Branch of the High Court, Liang Renjie, president of the Third Branch of the High Court, Luo Tong, president of the District Court, and Deng Zuyu, a friend of Mr. Wang, and Mrs. Zhu, Mr. Wang's wife, and more than a hundred others.

Personnel Arriving Together

Mr. Wang was wearing a long blue silk gown and a thick scarf around his neck. His complexion was slightly paler than when he returned home last time, but his spirits were very good. He shook hands with the welcomers on the ship to express his thanks. Then, he met with reporters from various newspapers on the ship. Immediately afterwards, he disembarked and went to the Hong'en Hospital for treatment. Those who accompanied Mr. Wang to Shanghai included Cheng Tiangu and Mr. Wang's attendants Xiao Jinfang, Zhu Xiaoshan, and Feng Zhizheng. Wei Daoming, the former Minister of Justice, will postpone his arrival in Shanghai for a few days because of unfinished business in Hong Kong.

Delivered a Speech

According to Mr. Wang, when he met with reporters from various newspapers on the ship, he gave a speech saying that he had decided to return home and had visited Mr. Hu Zhantang, chairman of the Central Executive Committee, and the Guangdong and Guangxi authorities in Guangdong. Of course, there was some discussion on national and private matters. As for the details, I will talk about them in person later. Because I have a slight cold en route, I have decided to go to the hospital for treatment immediately after disembarking. I will have to stay in the hospital for a few days. After my body recovers, I will go to Beijing. Whether I will go to Fenghua to visit President Chiang is still undecided. Mr. Hu Zhantang's body has gradually recovered to health. He will go north to Beijing to take office after the spring warmth. Mr. Wang then gave his observations on the European situation, saying that although the European situation is very tense, according to what I have observed, there will be no war. The authorities of various European countries are now trying to avoid war.

Appointment with Chiang

Last night, according to Mr. Wang's secretary Xiao Jinfang speaking to a reporter from Xin Sheng She, Mr. Wang had telegraphed Fenghua after arriving in Shanghai to report to Mr. Chiang, saying in essence that after arriving in Shanghai, he entered the hospital for treatment due to illness. As soon as his condition improves slightly, he will go to Beijing. Mr. Wang has a chronic nasal disease. He will relapse whenever he catches a cold. This decision to return home and arrive in Guangdong via Hong Kong was due to the long sea journey and fatigue, and the weather in Hong Kong and Guangdong was also cold, which caused his nasal disease to recur. The journey to Shanghai made it worse. The ship's doctor advised him that if he did not receive proper treatment, there was a risk of it spreading. Therefore, after arriving in Shanghai, he went to the Hong'en Hospital and asked Bi Gang, a famous ENT doctor in the hospital, for diagnosis and treatment. According to Bi Gang, the disease is not dangerous and can be expected to heal in four or five days if it is well treated. It is expected that Mr. Wang will be able to enter Beijing within a week.

Sun and Xu Express Condolences

Since Wang Chonghui arrived in Shanghai and entered the Hong'en Hospital, because he was afraid of the wind and cold, he followed the doctor's advice and declined all social engagements. Therefore, he declined banquets from Sun Ke, President of the Legislative Yuan, and others. Sun Ke, President of the Legislative Yuan, Xu Chongzhi, Vice President of the Control Yuan, and Niu Yongjian, Vice President of the Examination Yuan, first went to the Hong'en Hospital for a visit at about 1:00 p.m. However, because Mr. Wang was in poor spirits, they did not have a long talk and left after expressing their condolences. In addition, Cai Jingjun, Director of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, also went to visit him.

Zhang Gongquan Arrives in Shanghai to Talk About His Impressions of Inspecting the Guangdong-Hankou Railway

Zhang Gongquan, Minister of Railways, accompanied by secretaries Yang Yizhi and Gao Dajing, went to Hankou, Guangzhou, Guilin, and other places last month to inspect the current situation of the Guangdong-Hankou Railway. He has now completed his task. He arrived in Shanghai yesterday morning at 11:00 a.m. on the Italian postal ship Victoria. Mayor Wu's representative Secretary Tang Shixuan, Director Zhou Jue of the Foreign Affairs Office, Huang Boqiao of the Beijing-Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administration, Secretary Wang Zhinan of the Municipal Security Office, Zou Bingwen and Chen Xiangtao from the banking community, and Mr. Zhang's wife and dozens of others welcomed him. After disembarking, Mr. Zhang went straight back to his private residence and plans to go to Beijing to report to the ministry in one or two days. According to Mr. Zhang speaking to a reporter from the Central News Agency on the ship, his trip to Guangdong, Hankou, Guilin, and other places was purely to inspect the Guangdong-Hankou Railway. The result was very satisfactory. The various sections of the Guangdong-Hankou Railway will be connected in May and will be open to traffic in September or October. The Guangdong Provincial Government will designate Huangpu as a commercial port and plans to request the Ministry of Railways to allocate funds to build a branch line. This matter is related to the Guangdong-Hankou Railway itself and is currently being discussed. As for the news report that the Guangzhou-Kowloon Railway will be connected to the Guangdong-Hankou Railway, I am not aware of it. I did not discuss this with the Guangdong authorities during my visit to Guangdong. As for the construction of the Hunan-Guangxi Railway, the Ministry of Railways has this plan. How to proceed is still under discussion.

The guests and host enjoyed themselves until around 9:00 PM when the party ended. The Japanese Ambassador Instructs Japanese Residents Not to Damage National Dignity

According to the Japanese-language "Mainichi Shimbun," a welcome reception for Ambassador Arita was held in this port on the 21st, attended by over 300 Japanese officials and civilians. Ambassador Arita made the following remarks: "I am deeply regretful that I must return to my country so soon after taking office. During my sixteen-day stay in Nanjing, my meetings with key figures in Nanjing have given me a general understanding of the Chinese government authorities' intentions regarding the Sino-Japanese problem. The resolution of the Sino-Japanese problem will likely not be achieved overnight. However, the issue of China is extremely important to Japan and cannot be treated lightly. Therefore, we must seize every opportunity to work to adjust Sino-Japanese relations. I sincerely hope that residents will emphasize their character and refrain from any actions that may damage the nation's dignity."

The Director of the Sichuan Provincial Department of Finance, Liu Hangchen, Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday; Negotiating Public Bond Mortgages with Various Banks; Construction Bank Investing in the Chengdu-Chongqing Road Construction

Liu Hangchen, Director of the Sichuan Provincial Department of Finance, arrived in Shanghai from Beijing yesterday and is staying at a friend's place. Liu's visit is to negotiate the mortgage of 15 million yuan of Sichuan Post-Disaster Public Bonds with the banking community and to organize the Sichuan-Guizhou Railway Company to raise funds for the construction of the Chengdu-Chongqing Railway. The New News Agency reporter investigated and reported on these matters as follows:

Negotiating Public Bond Mortgages

In order to complete the bandit suppression work and post-disaster reconstruction in Sichuan Province, the Chairman of the Sichuan Provincial Government, Liu Xiang, requested the central government to issue 15 million yuan of the 25th Year of the Republic of China Sichuan Post-Disaster Reconstruction Public Bonds, which has been approved by the central government and is scheduled to be formally issued on April 1st. Sichuan Finance Director Liu Hangchen, in view of the urgent need for funds for financial consolidation and post-disaster affairs in Sichuan Province, came to Shanghai earlier this month to negotiate with the Central Bank for an advance loan of 2 million yuan to meet immediate needs, which has been approved by the Ministry of Finance. Liu's current visit to Shanghai is to continue negotiations with the Central, China, and Communications Banks regarding the mortgage of the public bonds. He is scheduled to visit the authorities of the three banks today to earnestly discuss the mortgage methods. Once a result is reached, he will collect the printed public bond certificates from the printing bureau and take them back to Sichuan for issuance. It is reported that after the central government's consolidation of Sichuan's finances, things may get on track when the 25th year begins.

Organizing the Railway Company

Regarding the construction of the Chengdu-Chongqing Railway, Lu Zuofu, Director of the Sichuan Provincial Department of Construction, prepared a plan and consulted with the Ministry of Railways. It was decided to organize the Sichuan-Guizhou Railway Company to be responsible for the construction. According to the New News Agency reporter, the organizational regulations of the Sichuan-Guizhou Railway Company were passed by the Executive Yuan's routine meeting on the 21st. The total amount of shares is set at 20 million yuan, divided into 200,000 shares. The Ministry of Railways and the Sichuan Provincial Government each recognize 22,500 shares, and the rest will be raised independently. The company may issue public bonds as appropriate to supplement construction funds and has decided to first build the main line from Chengdu to Chongqing and the branch line from Neijiang to Zigong. After completion, other lines will be expanded. Liu's visit to Shanghai is to conveniently contact the financial community for investment, so that the company can be established as soon as possible. It is also heard that Lu Zuofu, Director of the Sichuan Provincial Department of Construction, is scheduled to come to Shanghai soon to discuss the company's preparation matters with the financial and industrial sectors.

Construction of the Chengdu-Chongqing Railway

The construction funds for the Chengdu-Chongqing Railway were budgeted by Lu Zuofu, Director of the Sichuan Provincial Department of Construction, who also provided blueprints of the railway line to Railway Minister Zhang Jia'ao for instructions. It was approved and tentatively set at 48 million yuan in national currency. Lu had previously consulted with Song Zi'liang, General Manager of China Construction Bank, regarding an investment of 10 million yuan as construction funds for the road. In addition, a loan of 20 million yuan was pre-ordered from France for materials, so that construction could begin in the shortest possible time, with the aim of completing and opening the line to traffic within two years. The above loans are planned to be secured by the post-disaster public bonds issued on April 1st and a portion of the Ministry of Railways' third-phase public bonds. These loans will continue to be negotiated by Directors Liu and Lu and are expected to be successful.

Jianghai Customs Notice: Procedures for Claiming Foreign Goods; Effective from the 6th of Next Month

Paul Barentzen, Commissioner of Customs of the Jianghai Customs, in order to stipulate the procedures for claiming imported foreign goods stored in the wharves and warehouses of transport ships, recently issued Notice No. 1501, stating that starting from April 6th of this year, imported foreign goods stored in the wharves and warehouses of transport ships should be claimed according to the following regulations: All imported foreign goods that have been taxed and approved for release by the Customs must have the Customs-stamped bill of lading submitted to the customs officer stationed at the warehouse to verify that it matches the red inspection slip before they can be claimed. All imported foreign goods that have not been taxed and are reported for transfer or storage in the Customs warehouse must have the Customs-stamped transfer permit or storage permit submitted to the customs officer stationed at the warehouse for verification before they can be claimed. When necessary, goods removed from the warehouse should be re-inspected by customs officers. From the date of implementation of the aforementioned procedures, all goods that have been taxed and approved for release in the wharves and warehouses of steamships approved for direct storage of imported foreign goods must be removed within 48 hours (excluding Sundays and holidays) after the customs officer receives the red inspection slip. If the above-mentioned time limit is exceeded, the shipping company should transfer the goods elsewhere on behalf of the owner. All merchants should be informed accordingly. This notice is hereby issued.

Ministry of Finance Plans to Stabilize the Exchange Rate of Subsidiary Currency

According to the East China News Agency, after the Ministry of Finance implemented the new currency policy on November 4th of last year, it stipulated the exchange rate of subsidiary currency on the 9th of the same month: one legal tender yuan is equivalent to 3,000 copper coins or 12 dimes, and each dime is worth 500 copper coins. However, since the promulgation of this decree, there have still been those who outwardly complied but inwardly disobeyed. The exchange rate in Shanghai is even more inconsistent, with three phenomena: In the urban area, each yuan is exchanged for 3,050 copper coins or 12 dimes and 20 copper coins. In the French Concession, each legal tender yuan is exchanged for 2,980 to 3,000 copper coins or 10 dimes and 450 to 12 dimes. Furthermore, the exchange rates at tram stations, bus stations, etc., also change at any time, causing travelers to complain. The value of new subsidiary currency ranges from 9 dimes and 7 cents to 9 dimes and 9 cents. People feel deeply pained by the fluctuating exchange rates of miscellaneous coins and eagerly hope that the Ministry of Finance will have practical measures to deal with this. Therefore, the Ministry of Finance plans that during the implementation of the decimal system, those who deliberately manipulate exchange rates will be severely punished according to the law. On the one hand, more 1-dime, 2-dime, and 5-dime new subsidiary currency notes will be printed to supplement the deficiency of nickel coins.

The Election of Foreign Directors of the Shanghai Municipal Council Begins Today

Today and tomorrow (Monday and Tuesday) are the dates for foreign taxpayers in the Public Concession to vote for the foreign directors. The time is from 10:00 AM to 3:00 PM, without interruption at noon. There are two polling locations: one is the Shanghai Volunteer Corps Drill Hall, and the other is the Hongkou Police Station.
