Shen Bao This City Supplement

Talk

Shanghai Jews Commemorate National Fighters

— Zhou Ge

There are more than 500 Jews in Shanghai. On the morning of the 16th of this month at 10 o'clock, all the Jews in Shanghai held a grand commemorative parade at the Jewish General Assembly at No. 35 Moore Road to commemorate the 16th anniversary of the death of their national hero Troplerder and to promote the movement to return to Palestine.

We all know that the Jewish nation has lost their country for more than 2,500 years. Until now, they have no fixed territory (it is said that the Soviet Union already has a Jewish country). Their footprints are all over the world. Although a small number of them have manipulated some of the financial ruling power in the United Kingdom and the United States because they are good at doing business, the pain of losing their country is enough for you to suffer with just a contemptuous smile from others.

Yes, the Jews have lost their country for more than 2,500 years, but until now, they still have the idea of ​​returning to their country, which may be considered a "luxury." In the gathering on the 16th, the more than 500 Jews in Shanghai (remember, only more than 500!) had already armed their young people in preparation for the restoration of their country: divided into young children, teenagers, adults (divided into army and navy), women, and other teams. This heroic action is caused by the pain of losing their country. To us Chinese people who are about to become "quasi-slaves to the country" (?), it is really heartbreaking!

Arabs and Jews now live together in the ancient Jewish kingdom. In 1919, Troplerder returned to Palestine to carry out the national construction movement and was unfortunately killed by Arabs. Before being killed, Mr. Te and his 50 or so comrades had waged a fierce resistance. Before his death, Mr. Te said the following heroic words: "I am a Jewish nationalist, regardless of anything else, no class, no selfish desires, no self. I am a piece of iron and I am willing to be used for the country. If the country needs a wheel, I am a wheel. If the country needs a nail, a plow, or a sickle, I am it! Jewish nationalists are the crystallization of the country's wishes, and they sacrifice everything for the country!" These words are now deeply engraved in the hearts of the armed Jewish youths. The Jewish nation will never perish! "Even if Chu has only three households, Chu will surely destroy Qin." Now, isn't there much more than "three households" in the Jewish nation?

People who lost their country more than 2,500 years ago are still making every effort to prepare for the restoration of their country. We have not yet reached the point of losing our country.

The Green Island

— Ye Lai

——Travel Notes

On the fourth day of our voyage, we arrived at the port of a tall mountain peak

"That's the green island"! Look, what a beautiful island! Have you read "Investiture of the Gods"? Doesn't the old myth

Page 16

Are there many interesting fairylands described? Well, let's just assume that it is one of the three Penglai islands!"

The old uncle squinted his eyes and looked into the distance, patting my arm.

"The mountain peaks of the island country are green, and it is also green from a distance. Who would believe that those are the three Penglai islands in mythology? Look, lush grass is growing, decorating the huge and neat Western-style buildings, arranged level by level all the way up to the top, which is hidden in the clouds and mist, and the top of the mountain has become many charming illusions.

The sun is far away in the East China Sea, and all that is seen is a deeply affectionate rosy glow covering the magnificent island country, smiling like a virgin!

Look, the southwest side is Kowloon. Kowloon and the green island are like two sisters, beautiful and charming! Think about it, whoever has money to live here will enjoy happiness."

The old uncle pointed so much, nagging, but I didn't understand what it meant:

"Why? This is no longer our country. Maybe we have become slaves."

"Little Lai'er! Why do you still say those childish things?"

His face looked gloomy, like a defeated fairy in mythology, and his cramped face gradually trembled. He took a breath and looked at the deep green sea. —Many magnificent and large fireboats and long warships were anchored on the sea, as if glaring at the coast in protest. Some small steamships were floating and walking, spewing out white foam.

What he said was a little sentimental.

"This world is the same everywhere. The rich are with the rich, and they don't care about their faces or their motherland! Here, things are combined to form a special product of the current century. Of course, people without money may be stripped, and people without money are slaves here."

I understood, his words were like a bowl of cold water poured on my body, and my heart was also beating. That beautiful green island actually hides so many festering sores!

The small fireboat carried us into the port. Slowly, the old and the young stood side by side, leaning on the railing and kissing the fleeting sea breeze.

"Wait a moment, I'll take you to see the factory from a few years ago! That's where I worked. Little Lai'er, do you know? During the Hong Kong and Guangzhou general strike a few years ago, this place turned into a dead port. There was really no life, and the faces of all the rich people were anxious. I was also one of that group, and I would also lead my companions across the mountains, swim across the sea, and return to the provincial capital."

The old uncle was still telling his stories, an endless string of them, but the ship had arrived at the shore. The distant and long jetty and the tall Western-style houses seemed to have woken up, opened their mouths wide, and revealed chaotic sounds, waiting for the constantly incoming tourists to throw themselves into its embrace. The old uncle twisted my hand again:

"Let's go play, but there aren't any beautiful things like in the myth!"

That's right, I looked around strangely. Under the narrow arcade, there was still hiding in the shadows, and the two-story trams were walking wearily. Every shop was fluttering with: "Big Discount"! "Selling at Cost"!... The flags seemed to have flown in from somewhere else.

Unconsciously, we had run to the back of the mountain, looking at the green sea from the green meadow, and the virgin-like sun was shining on everything in the island country again.

Loneliness

— Zhu Mingxia

I can't remember how old I am now, but anyway, when I was very young, I suddenly felt lonely. The first time I felt lonely was in my mother's eyes.

It was a spring afternoon. The rural towns that specialize in estimating the business of farmers were so quiet during this busy farming season that there was not even a sound of people. Our house was farther away from the shop because there were more houses, so it was even quieter in the afternoon, so quiet that even the sound of a bird flapping its wings could be heard. The small patio was full of sunshine, but because there was not even a shadow, I didn't feel it. A clump of small grass was growing happily among the rubble.

My mother was sitting on a bamboo chair sewing clothes, and I was sitting on a small stool reading. I don't know if it was because the quiet air was forcing me not to open my mouth; or if I didn't want to break the calm air, neither of us said a word? After a long time, my mother suddenly hummed a song that I hadn't heard. The singing was so soft that it sounded like a low sigh. Just as the singing was getting lower and lower, suddenly the sound of "Ding Dang" "Ding Dang" came from a distance. This was the sound of the iron shop at the end of the town.

Originally, it was a whole piece of silence. At this time, the sound of hammering iron broke it and made the silence even thicker. At the same time, the smoke from the neighboring house cooking some snacks curled up gently. At this time, my mother suddenly put down the sewing in her hand and stared intently at the clump of small grass in the middle of the rubble. It was at this time that I suddenly saw something I had never seen before in my mother's eyes — "loneliness."

Like a heavy piece of lead pressing on my heart, I could no longer push it away.

Yes, at some times, I had forgotten about this "loneliness." But this time was not very long, and as time passed year after year, this piece of lead also became heavier and heavier year after year. Recently, this piece of lead has become so heavy that I can hardly carry it.

Generally speaking, loneliness starts in the afternoon, especially at night. As soon as the wrong yellow electric light comes on, this loneliness is always particularly aggravated. Huang Zhongze's poem "A hundred sorrows fall like shadows before the lamp" I think half of the so-called hundred sorrows here is loneliness.

If someone is knowledgeable, then he will probably always feel lonely. There are too many articles describing loneliness throughout history, but only one section by Mr. Lu Xun truly writes about loneliness:

"In a large Western-style building, there was no one else except me. I calmed down. The silence was as thick as wine, making me slightly drunk. Looking out the back window, there were many white spots in the bone-like chaos, which were clumps of graves; a deep yellow fire was the evening bell of Nanputuo Temple. In front of me, the sea and the sky were vast, and the dark catkins-like colors were about to pounce on my heart. I leaned on the stone railing and looked into the distance, listening to the sound of my own heart. All around seemed to be boundless sorrow, suffering, desolation, and death, but they were mixed with this loneliness, turning it into medicinal wine, adding color, adding flavor, adding fragrance..."

Because Mr. Lu Xun was not a weak person, he was able to chew on such thick loneliness. I don't know how many people in the world have committed suicide because of this simple loneliness?

Loneliness is not sadness, but it makes people feel more uncomfortable than sadness. What's more, when a person feels unbearable sadness, he has often come out from under the heavy pressure of loneliness.

The Night Watch

— Zhuang Ruiyuan

When the fire crackles in the stove, and the quilt gradually warms, it makes one have a greedy longing for solitude in an empty room.

Outside the window, the night wind blows hard, carrying the cold, arranging a piercing tune on the four or five wires at the top of the lamppost, playing it intensely. The night has some terror and some cold.

But what is even more terrifying and cold is the weary striking of the night watchman's clapper, floating sparsely in a troubled dream.

A clapper and a lantern together probe the bottomless third and fifth watches of the night.

The night traveler of the night watch, like a ghost, takes steps, steps as strange and quiet as the night. Terror and cold are also in his heart.

For an empty room, there is a greedy longing for solitude. For the desolate night watch, I hold a feeling of eager anticipation for a meeting.

In a troubled night, I caress the scars of a weary life, I futilely use rest to apply to the scars, futilely use quiet natural numbers to massage the pain; thus there is a heavy sigh, in a night troubled by sleeplessness.

Without an upsurge of sleepiness, but instead a feeling of closeness to the sparse sounds of the night watch, anticipating it with such eager feelings.

The night is without chaotic noises, as quiet as the endless sea. The sound of the clapper cast into the sea of night is like a stone cast into a dark puddle, densely spreading out sound waves as terrifying as the night.

The sound waves of the clapper, surging from a distant corner of a house, surge into my room, so my eardrums recount it to me again, and in my ear canals there are lingering, drowning notes, low, echoing notes.

The sound of the clapper gradually approaches, and then gradually fades away. I remember that the narrow street is curved, passing by this curved street, the narrow wooden bridge and the mud road lead straight past my house, and lie outside the window of the house.

Approaching the night watchman, the changing sound, and a weak paper lantern together, stir my eager heart, for no reason I swallow a sigh, a selfish sigh of some terror and some cold.

Facing the direction from which the strange night traveler comes, we brazenly prop up half our bodies, filtering through my sleepy eyes, watching leisurely and in astonishment, the ghost-like night traveler wearing a worn felt hat, the lazy, red lantern, and the monotonous sound of the clapper, desolately probing the bottomless night watch.

Like hearing the cry of a night food seller, I feel an infinite, profound taste, echoing low in the vacuum of emotions.

It is not that the sound of the night watch disturbs sleep, but rather that the sound of the night watch has a familiar feeling for me, a hypnotic effect.

Please - those sparse but familiar sounds of the night watch.

The sound of the night watch has gone away, leaving residual faint tones on the four or five wires at the top of the lamppost.

Movie News

Yangtze Holds Hundred Flowers Dance Festival

Since its opening, the Yangtze Ballroom has been praised by all sectors of society, so last year it increased seating once, but even now late guests still lack seats and the reception is inadequate, which is deeply regretted. The owner of the Yangtze, in view of this, immediately expanded the room, increasing a large number of seats, and renovated it to accommodate a large number of dancers. The project is about to be completed, and a Hundred Flowers Dance Festival is specially prepared to open on March 21st, lasting for seven days until the evening of the 27th, to provide entertainment for all sectors, and to record the new ballroom, and to thank customers for their patronage over the years. The initiation of this event is to examine the individual nature of each dancer in the hall, their movement and stillness, quality and inferiority, height and weight, and then determine which flower they should be made up as, so that people and this flower have sympathy and the same nature. The strong interest in this, appreciated by both the elegant and the vulgar, is precisely the idea of beauties like flowers for you to choose from. While dancing, the branches are radiant, the fragrance of the flowers is overflowing, leaning on the red and relying on the green, utterly infatuating, still hoping that ladies and gentlemen from all walks of life, poets and writers, will evaluate them one by one, in order to conform to the theme of beauties like flowers, and increase interest.
